            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Electromagnetism" title="Template talk:Electromagnetism">
             <abbr title="Discuss this template">
              t
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-edit">
            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Electromagnetism&amp;action=edit">
             <abbr title="Edit this template">
              e
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">
        physics
       </a>
       (particularly in
       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetism" title="Electromagnetism">
        electromagnetism
       </a>
       ) the
       <b>
        Lorentz force
       </b>
       is the combination of electric and magnetic
       <a href="/wiki/Force" title="Force">
        force
       </a>
       on a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Point_charge" title="Point charge">
        point charge
       </a>
       due to
       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_field" title="Electromagnetic field">
        electromagnetic fields
       </a>
       . A particle of charge
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       moving with velocity
       <b>
        v
       </b>
       in the presence of an
       <a href="/wiki/Electric_field" title="Electric field">
        electric field
       </a>
       <b>
        E
       </b>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_field" title="Magnetic field">
        magnetic field
       </a>
       <b>
        B
       </b>
       experiences a force
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =q\mathbf {E} +q\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                F
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               q
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                E
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mi>
               q
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                v
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ×
               <!-- × -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                B
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =q\mathbf {E} +q\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} }
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\mathbf  {F}}=q{\mathbf  {E}}+q{\mathbf  {v}}\times {\mathbf  {B}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ccc7325732c56e5caeacd2005cd803c9ed5e9d8d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:17.67ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       (in
       <a href="/wiki/International_System_of_Units" title="International System of Units">
        SI units
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-units_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-units-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-units2_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-units2-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ). Variations on this basic formula describe the magnetic force on a current-carrying wire (sometimes called
       <a href="#Force_on_a_current-carrying_wire">
        Laplace force
       </a>
       ), the
       <a href="/wiki/Electromotive_force" title="Electromotive force">
        electromotive force
       </a>
       in a wire loop moving through a magnetic field (an aspect of
       <a href="/wiki/Faraday%27s_law_of_induction" title="Faraday's law of induction">
        Faraday's law of induction
       </a>
       ), and the force on a charged particle which might be traveling near the
       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">
        speed of light
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">
        relativistic
       </a>
       form of the Lorentz force).
      </p>
      <p>
       The first derivation of the Lorentz force is commonly attributed to
       <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Heaviside" title="Oliver Heaviside">
        Oliver Heaviside
       </a>
       in 1889,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nahin_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nahin-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although other historians suggest an earlier origin in an 1865 paper by
       <a href="/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell" title="James Clerk Maxwell">
        James Clerk Maxwell
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huray_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Huray-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Lorentz" title="Hendrik Lorentz">
        Hendrik Lorentz
       </a>
       derived it in 1895,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dahl_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dahl-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a few years after Heaviside.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Equation">
        Equation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorentz_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Equation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Charged_particle">
        Charged particle
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorentz_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Charged particle">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lorentz_force_particle.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="345" data-file-width="325" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lorentz_force_particle.svg/200px-Lorentz_force_particle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lorentz_force_particle.svg/300px-Lorentz_force_particle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lorentz_force_particle.svg/400px-Lorentz_force_particle.svg.png 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lorentz_force_particle.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Lorentz force
         <b>
          F
         </b>
         on a
         <a href="/wiki/Charged_particle" title="Charged particle">
          charged particle
         </a>
         (of charge
         <i>
          q
         </i>
         ) in motion (instantaneous velocity
         <b>
          v
         </b>
         ). The
         <a href="/wiki/Electric_field" title="Electric field">
          <b>
           E
          </b>
          field
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_field" title="Magnetic field">
          <b>
           B
          </b>
          field
         </a>
         vary in space and time.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The force
       <b>
        F
       </b>
       acting on a particle of
       <a href="/wiki/Electric_charge" title="Electric charge">
        electric charge
       </a>
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       with instantaneous velocity
       <b>
        v
       </b>
       , due to an external electric field
       <b>
        E
       </b>
       and magnetic field
       <b>
        B
       </b>
       , is given by (in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI_units" title="SI units">
        SI units
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-units_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-units-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ):
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson2_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jackson2-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <table cellpadding="5" style="border:2px solid #50C878;background: #ECFCF4; text-align: center;">
         <tr>
          <td>
           <p>
            <span class="mwe-math-element">
             <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
              <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =q(\mathbf {E} +\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} )}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
               <semantics>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    F
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mo>
                   =
                  </mo>
                  <mi>
                   q
                  </mi>
                  <mo stretchy="false">
                   (
                  </mo>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    E
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mo>
                   +
                  </mo>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    v
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mo>
                   ×
                   <!-- × -->
                  </mo>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    B
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mo stretchy="false">
                   )
                  </mo>
                 </mstyle>
                </mrow>
                <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
                 {\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =q(\mathbf {E} +\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} )}
                </annotation>
               </semantics>
              </math>
             </span>
             <img alt="\mathbf {F} =q(\mathbf {E} +\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} )" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a3dd99e3bd55cbeff1cd2506d944405f3efa9e0c" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.41ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
            </span>
           </p>
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <big>
        ×
       </big>
       is the vector cross product. All boldface quantities are vectors. More explicitly stated:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {F} (\mathbf {r} ,\mathbf {\dot {r}} ,t,q)=q[\mathbf {E} (\mathbf {r} ,t)+\mathbf {\dot {r}} \times \mathbf {B} (\mathbf {r} ,t)]}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                F
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                r
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mover>
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  r
                 </mi>
                 <mo mathvariant="bold">
                  ˙
                  <!-- ˙ -->
                 </mo>
                </mover>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
              <mi>
               t
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
              <mi>
               q
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               q
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               [
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                E
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                r
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
              <mi>
               t
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mover>
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  r
                 </mi>
                 <mo mathvariant="bold">
                  ˙
                  <!-- ˙ -->
                 </mo>
                </mover>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ×
               <!-- × -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                B
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                r
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
              <mi>
               t
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               ]
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \mathbf {F} (\mathbf {r} ,\mathbf {\dot {r}} ,t,q)=q[\mathbf {E} (\mathbf {r} ,t)+\mathbf {\dot {r}} \times \mathbf {B} (\mathbf {r} ,t)]}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbf {F} (\mathbf {r} ,\mathbf {\dot {r}} ,t,q)=q[\mathbf {E} (\mathbf {r} ,t)+\mathbf {\dot {r}} \times \mathbf {B} (\mathbf {r} ,t)]}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/09e1b5355b1ba774c429c04f7422db91a34ae831" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:36.649ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       in which
       <b>
        r
       </b>
       is the position vector of the charged particle,
       <i>
        t
       </i>
       is time, and the overdot is a time derivative.
      </p>
      <p>
       A positively charged particle will be accelerated in the
       <i>
        same
       </i>
       linear orientation as the
       <b>
        E
       </b>
       field, but will curve perpendicularly to both the instantaneous velocity vector
       <b>
        v
       </b>
       and the
       <b>
        B
       </b>
       field according to the
       <a href="/wiki/Right-hand_rule" title="Right-hand rule">
        right-hand rule
       </a>
       (in detail, if the fingers of the right hand are extended to point in the direction of
       <b>
        v
       </b>
       and are then curled to point in the direction of
       <b>
        B
       </b>
       , then the extended thumb will point in the direction of
       <b>
        F
       </b>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       The term
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       <b>
        E
       </b>
       is called the
       <b>
        electric force
       </b>
       , while the term
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       <b>
        v
       </b>
       <big>
        ×
       </big>
       <b>
        B
       </b>
       is called the
       <b>
        magnetic force
       </b>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Griffiths1_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Griffiths1-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to some definitions, the term "Lorentz force" refers specifically to the formula for the magnetic force,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Griffiths2_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Griffiths2-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with the
       <i>
        total
       </i>
       electromagnetic force (including the electric force) given some other (nonstandard) name. This article will
       <i>
        not
       </i>
       follow this nomenclature: In what follows, the term "Lorentz force" will refer to the expression for the total force.
      </p>
      <p>
       The magnetic force component of the Lorentz force manifests itself as the force that acts on a current-carrying wire in a magnetic field. In that context, it is also called the
       <a href="#Force_on_a_current-carrying_wire">
        Laplace force
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Lorentz force is a force exerted by the electromagnetic field on the charged particle, that is, it is the rate at which linear momentum is transferred from the electromagnetic field to the particle. Associated with it is the power which is the rate at which energy is transferred from the electromagnetic field to the particle. That power is
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {v} \cdot \mathbf {F} =q\,\mathbf {v} \cdot \mathbf {E} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                v
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ⋅
               <!-- ⋅ -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                F
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               q
              </mi>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                v
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ⋅
               <!-- ⋅ -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                E
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \mathbf {v} \cdot \mathbf {F} =q\,\mathbf {v} \cdot \mathbf {E} }
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbf {v} \cdot \mathbf {F} =q\,\mathbf {v} \cdot \mathbf {E} }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/77c9e96e8529d82b462687e8ff05763be8773e78" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:14.175ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
        .
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Notice that the magnetic field does not contribute to the power because the magnetic force is always perpendicular to the velocity of the particle.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Continuous_charge_distribution">
        Continuous charge distribution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorentz_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Continuous charge distribution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lorentz_force_continuum.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="348" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lorentz_force_continuum.svg/200px-Lorentz_force_continuum.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lorentz_force_continuum.svg/300px-Lorentz_force_continuum.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lorentz_force_continuum.svg/400px-Lorentz_force_continuum.svg.png 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lorentz_force_continuum.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Lorentz force (per unit 3-volume)
         <b>
          f
         </b>
         on a continuous
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charge_distribution" title="Charge distribution">
          charge distribution
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Charge_density" title="Charge density">
          charge density
         </a>
         ρ) in motion. The 3-
         <a href="/wiki/Current_density" title="Current density">
          current density
         </a>
         <b>
          J
         </b>
         corresponds to the motion of the charge element
         <i>
          dq
         </i>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Volume_element" title="Volume element">
          volume element
         </a>
         <i>
          dV
         </i>
         and varies throughout the continuum.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       For a continuous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charge_distribution" title="Charge distribution">
        charge distribution
       </a>
       in motion, the Lorentz force equation becomes:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathrm {d} \mathbf {F} =\mathrm {d} q\left(\mathbf {E} +\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} \right)\,\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                d
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                F
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                d
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               q
              </mi>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <mrow>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  E
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  v
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 ×
                 <!-- × -->
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  B
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
               <mo>
                )
               </mo>
              </mrow>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \mathrm {d} \mathbf {F} =\mathrm {d} q\left(\mathbf {E} +\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} \right)\,\!}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\mathrm {d} \mathbf {F} =\mathrm {d} q\left(\mathbf {E} +\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} \right)\,\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ef49a0e419262822b08e57a3efb00abd4bef723b" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:21.769ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <i>
        d
       </i>
       <b>
        F
       </b>
       is the force on a small piece of the charge distribution with charge
       <i>
        dq
       </i>
       . If both sides of this equation are divided by the volume of this small piece of the charge distribution
       <i>
        dV
       </i>
       , the result is:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {f} =\rho \left(\mathbf {E} +\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} \right)\,\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                f
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <mrow>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  E
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  v
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 ×
                 <!-- × -->
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  B
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
               <mo>
                )
               </mo>
              </mrow>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \mathbf {f} =\rho \left(\mathbf {E} +\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} \right)\,\!}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\mathbf {f} =\rho \left(\mathbf {E} +\mathbf {v} \times \mathbf {B} \right)\,\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1b1b493286996a2c84353154a3b1926f37b01248" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:18.687ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <b>
        f
       </b>
       is the
       <i>
        force density
       </i>
       (force per unit volume) and
       <i>
        ρ
       </i>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Charge_density" title="Charge density">
        charge density
       </a>
       (charge per unit volume). Next, the
       <a href="/wiki/Current_density" title="Current density">
        current density
       </a>
       corresponding to the motion of the charge continuum is
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {J} =\rho \mathbf {v} \,\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                J
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                v
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \mathbf {J} =\rho \mathbf {v} \,\!}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\mathbf {J} =\rho \mathbf {v} \,\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f7faeeea0907bb6895d45b01860d5cde4564136e" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:7.479ex; height:2.676ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       so the continuous analogue to the equation is
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Electrodynamics_1999_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Electrodynamics_1999-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <table cellpadding="6" style="border:2px solid #0073CF;background: #F5FFFA; text-align: center;">
         <tr>
          <td>
           <p>
            <span class="mwe-math-element">
             <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
              <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {f} =\rho \mathbf {E} +\mathbf {J} \times \mathbf {B} \,\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
               <semantics>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    f
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mo>
                   =
                  </mo>
                  <mi>
                   ρ
                   <!-- ρ -->
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    E
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mo>
                   +
                  </mo>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    J
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mo>
                   ×
                   <!-- × -->
                  </mo>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    B
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mspace width="thinmathspace">
                  </mspace>
                  <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
                  </mspace>
                 </mstyle>
                </mrow>
                <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
                 {\displaystyle \mathbf {f} =\rho \mathbf {E} +\mathbf {J} \times \mathbf {B} \,\!}
                </annotation>
               </semantics>
              </math>
             </span>
             <img alt="\mathbf {f} =\rho \mathbf {E} +\mathbf {J} \times \mathbf {B} \,\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6755b3f463c3c55c2d984a245f0d8047820b0463" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:16.46ex; height:2.676ex;"/>
            </span>
           </p>
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The total force is the
       <a href="/wiki/Volume_integral" title="Volume integral">
        volume integral
       </a>
       over the charge distribution:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =\iiint \!(\rho \mathbf {E} +\mathbf {J} \times \mathbf {B} )\,\mathrm {d} V.\,\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                F
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mo>
               ∭
               <!-- ∭ -->
              </mo>
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                E
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                J
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ×
               <!-- × -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                B
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="normal">
                d
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               V
              </mi>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =\iiint \!(\rho \mathbf {E} +\mathbf {J} \times \mathbf {B} )\,\mathrm {d} V.\,\!}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\mathbf {F} =\iiint \!(\rho \mathbf {E} +\mathbf {J} \times \mathbf {B} )\,\mathrm {d} V.\,\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a4c27f2bf3f9387ae121066348dee9bba0bfdcff" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:27.226ex; height:5.676ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       By eliminating ρ and
       <b>
        J
       </b>
       , using
       <a href="/wiki/Maxwell%27s_equations" title="Maxwell's equations">
        Maxwell's equations
       </a>
       , and manipulating using the theorems of
       <a href="/wiki/Vector_calculus" title="Vector calculus">
        vector calculus
       </a>
       , this form of the equation can be used to derive the
       <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_stress_tensor" title="Maxwell stress tensor">
        Maxwell stress tensor
       </a>
       <b>
        σ
       </b>
       , in turn this can be combined with the
       <a href="/wiki/Poynting_vector" title="Poynting vector">
        Poynting vector
       </a>
       <b>
        S
       </b>
       to obtain the
       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_stress%E2%80%93energy_tensor" title="Electromagnetic stress–energy tensor">
        electromagnetic stress–energy tensor
       </a>
       <b>
        T
       </b>
       used in
       <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">
        general relativity
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Electrodynamics_1999_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Electrodynamics_1999-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In terms of
       <b>
        σ
       </b>
       and
       <b>
        S
       </b>
       , another way to write the Lorentz force (per unit volume) is
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Electrodynamics_1999_9-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Electrodynamics_1999-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {f} =\nabla \cdot {\boldsymbol {\sigma }}-{\dfrac {1}{c^{2}}}{\dfrac {\partial \mathbf {S} }{\partial t}}\,\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                f
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi mathvariant="normal">
               ∇
               <!-- ∇ -->
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ⋅
               <!-- ⋅ -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">
                σ
                <!-- σ -->
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
                <mfrac>
                 <mn>
                  1
                 </mn>
                 <msup>
                  <mi>
                   c
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mn>
                    2
                   </mn>
                  </mrow>
                 </msup>
                </mfrac>
               </mstyle>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
                <mfrac>
                 <mrow>
                  <mi mathvariant="normal">
                   ∂
                   <!-- ∂ -->
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    S
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow>
                  <mi mathvariant="normal">
                   ∂
                   <!-- ∂ -->
                  </mi>
                  <mi>
                   t
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </mfrac>
               </mstyle>
              </mrow>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \mathbf {f} =\nabla \cdot {\boldsymbol {\sigma }}-{\dfrac {1}{c^{2}}}{\dfrac {\partial \mathbf {S} }{\partial t}}\,\!}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\mathbf {f} =\nabla \cdot {\boldsymbol {\sigma }}-{\dfrac {1}{c^{2}}}{\dfrac {\partial \mathbf {S} }{\partial t}}\,\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/31415b76d69c051b65ebfb14738ca478955c66dd" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:19.125ex; height:5.676ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <i>
        c
       </i>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">
        speed of light
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nabla_symbol" title="Nabla symbol">
        ∇
       </a>
       · denotes the divergence of a
       <a href="/wiki/Tensor_field" title="Tensor field">
        tensor field
       </a>
       . Rather than the amount of charge and its velocity in electric and magnetic fields, this equation relates the
       <a href="/wiki/Energy_flux" title="Energy flux">
        energy flux
       </a>
       (flow of
       <i>
        energy
       </i>
       per unit time per unit distance) in the fields to the force exerted on a charge distribution. See
       <a href="/wiki/Covariant_formulation_of_classical_electromagnetism#Charge_continuum" title="Covariant formulation of classical electromagnetism">
        Covariant formulation of classical electromagnetism
       </a>
       for more details.
      </p>
      <p>
       The density of power associated with the Lorentz force in a material medium is
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {J} \cdot \mathbf {E} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                J
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ⋅
               <!-- ⋅ -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                E

            </mrow>

          </math>

        </span>
        .
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       If we separate the total charge and total current into their free and bound parts, we get that the density of the Lorentz force is
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {f} =(\rho _{f}-\nabla \cdot \mathbf {P} )\mathbf {E} +(\mathbf {J} _{f}+\nabla \times \mathbf {M} +{\frac {\partial \mathbf {P} }{\partial t}})\times \mathbf {B} }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                f
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>

                <!-- ρ -->
               </mi>

               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>

               ∇
               <!-- ∇ -->
              </mi>

              </mo>

               <mi mathvariant="bold">

               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo stretchy="false">

              </mo>

              </mo>
              <mo stretchy="false">

              </mo>

               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="bold">

               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>

              <mo>
               +
              </mo>

               ∇
               <!-- ∇ -->
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ×
               <!-- × -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">

      <p>
       where: ρ
       <sub>
        f
       </sub>
       is the density of free charge;
       <i>
        P
       </i>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Polarization_density" title="Polarization density">
        polarization density
       </a>
       ;
       <i>
        J
       </i>
       <sub>
        f
       </sub>
       is the density of free current; and
       <i>

       </i>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Magnetization" title="Magnetization">
        magnetization
       </a>
       density. In this way, the Lorentz force can explain the torque applied to a permanent magnet by the magnetic field. The density of the associated power is
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Equation_in_cgs_units">
        Equation in cgs units
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorentz_force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Equation in cgs units">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The above-mentioned formulae use
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI_units" title="SI units">
        SI units
       </a>
       which are the most common among experimentalists, technicians, and engineers. In
       <a href="/wiki/Gaussian_units" title="Gaussian units">
        cgs-Gaussian units
       </a>
       , which are somewhat more common among theoretical physicists, one has instead
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =q_{\mathrm {cgs} }\left(\mathbf {E} _{\mathrm {cgs} }+{\frac {\mathbf {v} }{c}}\times \mathbf {B} _{\mathrm {cgs} }\right).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

                F
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                q
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  c
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  g
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  s
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <mrow>
                <msub>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi mathvariant="bold">
                   E
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="normal">
                    c
                   </mi>
                   <mi mathvariant="normal">

                   </mi>
                   <mi mathvariant="normal">
                    s
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </mrow>
                </msub>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mfrac>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi mathvariant="bold">
                    v
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mi>
                   c
                  </mi>
                 </mfrac>
                </mrow>
                <mo>

                 <!-- × -->
                </mo>

                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi mathvariant="bold">
                   B

                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

             {\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =q_{\mathrm {cgs} }\left(\mathbf {E} _{\mathrm {cgs} }+{\frac {\mathbf {v} }{c}}\times \mathbf {B} _{\mathrm {cgs} }\right).}
            </annotation>

        </span>

      <p>
       where
       <i>

       <sub>

       </sub>

       </a>
